	\item  if \(k\in\calS_{-0}\), \(i\in\mathcal S_+\), \(j\in\calS_+\cup\calS_{+0}\), 
	\begin{align}
                	\Big|&\int_{x=0}^\Delta \widehat{f}_{m,-0,+}^{\ell_0}(\lambda)(x,i,j_1,k_1,\dots,j_m,k_m,j;x_0,k)\psi(x) \wrt x\nonumber 
		\\&\qquad{} -\int_{x=0}^\Delta \widehat \mu_{m,-0,+}^{\ell_0}(\lambda)(x,i,j_1,k_1,\dots,j_m,k_m,j;x_0,k)\psi(x)\wrt x \Big| \nonumber
	\\&\leq \begin{cases} |r_{10}^{(p)}|, & m=0 \\ (|r_8(2m)|+|r_5(2m)|+|r_6(2m)| + (2m-1)|r_4(2m)|)\Delta F & m \geq 1 \end{cases}  \label{eqn: MMv}
	\end{align}
	\item {if \(k\in\calS_{-0}\), \(i\in\mathcal S_+\), \(j\in\calS_-\cup\calS_{-0}\), }
	\begin{align}
                	&\Big|\int_{x=0}^\Delta \widehat{f}_{m,-0,-}^{\ell_0}(\lambda)(x,i,j_1,k_1,\dots,k_m,j_{m+1},j;x_0,k)\psi(x)\wrt x\nonumber 
                	\\&\qquad{} -\int_{x=0}^\Delta \widehat \mu_{m,-0,-}^{\ell_0}(\lambda)(x,i,j_1,k_1,\dots,k_m,j_{m+1},j;x_0,k)\psi(x)\wrt x\Big|\nonumber 
	\\&\leq   (|r_8(2m+1)|+|r_5(2m+1)|+|r_6(2m+1)| + 2m|r_4(2m+1)|)\Delta F,\,  m \geq 0   \label{eqn: MMv22}
	\end{align}
	\item {if \(k\in\calS_{+0}\), \(i\in\mathcal S_-\), \(j\in\calS_+\cup\calS_{+0}\),}
	\begin{align}
                	&\Big|\int_{x=0}^\Delta \widehat{f}_{m,+0,+}^{\ell_0}(\lambda)(x,i,k_1,j_1,\dots,j_m,k_{m+1},j;x_0,k)\psi(x) \wrt x \nonumber 
                	\\&\qquad{} - \int_{x=0}^\Delta \widehat \mu_{m,+0,+}^{\ell_0}(\lambda)(x,i,k_1,j_1,\dots,j_m,k_{m+1},j;x_0,k)\psi(x) \wrt x\Big| \nonumber 
	\\&\leq   (|r_8(2m+1)|+|r_5(2m+1)|+|r_6(2m+1)| + 2m|r_4(2m+1)|)\Delta F,\,  m \geq 0   \label{eqn: MMv222}
	\end{align}
	\item {and if \(k\in\calS_{+0}\), \(i\in\mathcal S_-\), \(j\in\calS_-\cup\calS_{-0}\),}
	\begin{align}
                	&\Big|\int_{x=0}^\Delta \widehat{f}_{m,+0,-}^{\ell_0}(\lambda)(x,i,k_1,j_1,\dots,k_{m},j_{m},j;x_0,k)\psi(x) \wrt x\nonumber 
                	\\&\qquad{}-\int_{x=0}^\Delta \widehat{\mu}_{m,+0,-}^{\ell_0}(\lambda)(x,i,k_1,j_1,\dots,k_{m},j_{m},j;x_0,k)\psi(x)\wrt x\Big| \nonumber 
	\\&\leq \begin{cases}  |r_{10}^{(p)}|, & m=0 \\( |r_8(2m)|+|r_5(2m)|+|r_6(2m)| + (2m-1)|r_4(2m)|)\Delta F & m \geq 1. \end{cases}\label{eqn: MMv2}
	\end{align}
	\end{enumerate}
\end{cor}
%For \(r_2\) we have suppressed the dependence of \(r_2\) on \(p\) for simplicity here. When this dependence needs to be made explicit we write \(r_2^{(p)}\). 
\begin{proof} 
	For (\ref{eqn: ++}) and (\ref{eqn: --}) and \(m= 0\) apply Lemma~\ref{lem: Dcoajc} to the differences on the left-hand sides.
	
	For (\ref{eqn: ++}) and (\ref{eqn: --}) and \(m\geq 1\) apply Corollary~\ref{eqn: lafkjebjcbbalbvvbrb} to the differences on the left-hand sides.
	
	For (\ref{eqn: +-}) and (\ref{eqn: -+}) apply Corollary~\ref{eqn: lafkjebjcbbalbvvbrb} to the differences on the left-hand sides.
	
	For (\ref{eqn: MMv}) and (\ref{eqn: MMv2}) and \(m= 0\) apply Corollary~\ref{cor: Dcoajc} to the differences on the left-hand sides.
	
	For (\ref{eqn: MMv}) and (\ref{eqn: MMv2}) and \(m\geq 1\) apply Corollary~\ref{cor: fljm7778} to the differences on the left-hand sides.
	
	For (\ref{eqn: MMv22}) and (\ref{eqn: MMv222}) apply Corollary~\ref{cor: fljm7778} to the differences on the left-hand sides.
\end{proof}
These bounds are enough to show the weak convergence (in space and time) of the QBD-RAP scheme to the fluid queue on the event on the event that there is no change of level, and on a given partition as described in (\ref{eqn: 63})-(\ref{eqn: density part +}). Since the state space of the phases, \(\mathcal S\), is finite, then the same bounds show convergence when we sum over all possible phases at times \(\{\Sigma_m\}\) and \(\{\Gamma_m\}\). We formalise this with Corollary~\ref{cor: k}, below.
%These error bounds are enough to show the convergence as \(p\to\infty\) of expectations of \(\psi(x)\) with respect to the Laplace transforms with respect to time of (\ref{eqn: approx end conv})-(\ref{eqn: 67}) to the Laplace transforms with respect to time of (\ref{eqn: density part +})-(\ref{eqn: 63}), respectively. Moreover, since the sums in (\ref{eqn: loop mu})-(\ref{eqn: many eqns mu}) and (\ref{eqn: oihg87576})-(\ref{eqn: many eqns}) are finite and the Laplace transform is a Linear operator, then these bounds also show the converge as \(p\to \infty\) of the Laplace transforms with respect to time of (\ref{eqn: oihg87576})-(\ref{eqn: many eqns}) to the Laplace transforms with respect to time of (\ref{eqn: loop mu})-(\ref{eqn: many eqns mu}), respectively. 

\begin{cor}\label{cor: k}
	For \(q \in \{+,-,+0,-0\}\), \(r\in\{+,-\}\), \(i\in\calS_q\), \(j\in\calS_r\), \(x\in\calD_{\ell_0,j}\), \(x_0\in\calD_{\ell_0,i}\), \(\ell_0\in\mathcal K, \ell_0\notin\{-1,K+1\}\), \(m\geq 0\), \(\lambda > 0\), then 
	\begin{align}
		\left|\int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}}\widehat \mu_{m,p,q}^{\ell_0}(\lambda)( x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x)\wrt x - \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}}\widehat f^{\ell_0}_{m,p,q}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x) \wrt x\right| \to 0 \label{eqnALKJV}
	\end{align}
	as \(p\to\infty\). 
%	\begin{align}
%            	&\left|\int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}}\widehat \mu_{m,+,+}^{\ell_0}(\lambda)( x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x)\wrt x - \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}}\widehat f^{\ell_0}_{m,+,+}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i)\right|\psi(x) \wrt x \nonumber 
%%	\\&\qquad{}\leq \begin{cases}
%%			R_{V,2} GF + \varepsilon GF, & m = 0, \\
%%			|r_9(2m)||\calS_+|^m|\calS_-|^m,  &  m\geq 1,
%%			\end{cases} \label{eqn: mm}
%            	%
%            	\\&\left|\int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}}\widehat \mu^{\ell_0}_{m+1,+,-}(\lambda)( x, j; x_0,i)\psi(x)\wrt x-\int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}}\widehat f^{\ell_0}_{m+1,+,-}(\lambda)(x, j; x_0,i)\wrt x\right|  \nonumber 
%	\\&\qquad{}\leq |r_9(2m+1)||\calS_+|^m|\calS_-|^{m+1}
%	\\&\left|\int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}}\widehat \mu^{\ell_0}_{m+1,-,+}(\lambda)( x, j; x_0,i)\psi(x) \wrt x - \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}}\widehat f^{\ell_0}_{m+1,-,+}(\lambda)(x, j; x_0,i)\psi(x)\wrt x\right|  \nonumber 
%	\\&\qquad{}\leq |r_9(2m+1)||\calS_+|^{m+1}|\calS_-|^{m}
%            	\\&\left|\int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}}\widehat \mu^{\ell_0}_{m,-,-}(\lambda)( x, j; x_0,i)\wrt x -\int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} \widehat f^{\ell_0}_{m,-,-}(\lambda)(x, j; x_0,i)\wrt x \right|  \nonumber 
%	\\&\qquad{}\leq \begin{cases}
%			R_{V,2} GF + \varepsilon GF, & m = 0 \\
%			|r_9(2m)||\calS_+|^m|\calS_-|^m,  &  m\geq 1,
%			\end{cases} \label{eqn: aaa}
%        \end{align}
%        where \(r_9(m) = (|r_5(m)| + |r_6(m)| + (m-1)|r_4(m)|)\Delta F\). Moreover, 
%        \begin{align}
%            	\nonumber&\left|\int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}}\widehat \mu_{m,+0,+}^{\ell_0}(\lambda)( x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x)\wrt x - \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}}\widehat f^{\ell_0}_{m,+0,+}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x)\wrt x\right| \\&\leq \begin{cases}
%			|r_{10}^{(p)}|, & m = 0, \\
%			|r_9(2m)||\calS_+|^{m+1}|\calS_-|^m + (|r_9(2m+1)|+|r_8(2m+1)|\Delta F)|\calS_+|^{m+1}|\calS_-|^{m+1},  &  m\geq 1,
%			\end{cases} \label{eqn: mmc}
%            	%
%            	\\\nonumber&\left|\int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}}\widehat \mu^{\ell_0}_{m+1,+0,-}(\lambda)( x, j; x_0,i)\psi(x)\wrt x-\int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}}\widehat f^{\ell_0}_{m+1,+0,-}(\lambda)(x, j; x_0,i)\psi(x)\wrt x\right| 
%	\\&\leq |r_9(2m+1)||\calS_+|^{m+1}|\calS_-|^{m+1} + (|r_9(2m)|+|r_8(2m)|)|\calS_+|^m|\calS_-|^{m+1}
%	\\\nonumber&\left|\int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}}\widehat \mu^{\ell_0}_{m+1,-0,+}(\lambda)( x, j; x_0,i)\psi(x)\wrt x - \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}}\widehat f^{\ell_0}_{m+1,-0,+}(\lambda)(x, j; x_0,i)\psi(x)\wrt x\right|
%	\\&\leq |r_9(2m+1)||\calS_+|^{m+1}|\calS_-|^{m+1} + (|r_9(2m)|+|r_8(2m)|)|\calS_+|^{m+1}|\calS_-|^{m} 
%	\\\nonumber&\left|\int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}}\widehat \mu^{\ell_0}_{m,-0,-}(\lambda)( x, j; x_0,i)\psi(x)\wrt x -\int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}}\widehat f^{\ell_0}_{m,-0,-}(\lambda)(x, j; x_0,i)\psi(x)\wrt x\right| 
%	\\&\leq \begin{cases}
%			 |r_{10}^{(p)}|, & m = 0 \\
%			|r_9(2m)||\calS_+|^{m}|\calS_-|^{m+1} + (|r_9(2m+1)|+|r_8(2m+1)|)|\Delta F\calS_+|^{m+1}|\calS_-|^{m+1},  &  m\geq 1.
%			\end{cases} \label{eqn: aaac}
%        \end{align}
\end{cor}
\begin{proof}
%From (\ref{eqn: oihg87576}), \(f_{m,+,+}^{\ell_0}(x,j;x_0,i)\) is a finite sum of terms \(f^{\ell_0}_{m,+,+}(\lambda)( x, j_1,k_1,\dots,j_m,k_m, j; x_0,i)\), and since the Laplace transform is a linear operator, then 
%            \begin{align}
%            	\widehat f^{\ell_0}_{m,+,+}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i) &:= \sum_{j_1\in\mathcal S_-} \sum_{k_1\in\mathcal S_+}\dots \sum_{j_m\in\mathcal S_-}\sum_{k_m\in\mathcal S_+}  \widehat f^{\ell_0}_{m,+,+}(\lambda)( x, j_1,k_1,\dots,j_m,k_m, j; x_0,i).\nonumber% \label{eqn: ghat1}  
%            \end{align}
%            Similarly, 
%             \begin{align}
%            	\widehat \mu^{\ell_0}_{m,+,+}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i) &:= \sum_{j_1\in\mathcal S_-} \sum_{k_1\in\mathcal S_+}\dots \sum_{j_m\in\mathcal S_-}\sum_{k_m\in\mathcal S_+}  \widehat \mu^{\ell_0}_{m,+,+}(\lambda)( x, j_1,k_1,\dots,j_m,k_m, j; x_0,i). \nonumber%\label{eqn: muhat1}  
%            \end{align}
	We prove the result for \(q=r=+\) only, with the proofs for the other cases being analogous. 
	
	By (\ref{eqn: mu advh}) and (\ref{eqn: f advh}) and the triangle inequality, 
            \begin{align*}
            	&\left| \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} \widehat f^{\ell_0}_{m,+,+}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x)\wrt x -  \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} \widehat \mu^{\ell_0}_{m,+,+}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x)\wrt x\right|
		\\&\leq \sum_{j_1\in\mathcal S_-} \sum_{k_1\in\mathcal S_+}\dots \sum_{j_m\in\mathcal S_-}\sum_{k_m\in\mathcal S_+} \Big|  \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} \widehat f^{\ell_0}_{m,+,+}(\lambda)( x, j_1,k_1,\dots,j_m,k_m, j; x_0,i) \psi(x)\wrt x
		\\&\quad{}- \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} \widehat \mu^{\ell_0}_{m,+,+}(\lambda)( x, j_1,k_1,\dots,j_m,k_m, j; x_0,i)\psi(x)\wrt x \Big|
           %
		\\&\leq  \begin{cases}
			R_{V,2} GF + \varepsilon GF & m = 0 \\
			(|r_5(2m)| + |r_6(2m)| + 2m|r_4(2m)|)\Delta F |\calS_+|^m|\calS_-|^m  &  m\geq 1.
			\end{cases}
        \end{align*}
         since, by Corollary~\ref{cor: lst diff}, each term in the sum is bounded by either \(R_{V,2} GF + \varepsilon GF\) for \(m=0\) or by \((|r_5(2m)| + |r_6(2m)| + 2m|r_4(2m)|)|\Delta F \) for \(m\geq 0\). 
\end{proof}

%Recall that the goal is to show error bounds for the difference between the Laplace transform with respect to time of (\ref{eqn: approx to sojourn}) and the Laplace transform with respect to time of (\ref{eqn: trie thingy}).
%Since 
%\[\int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} f^{\ell_0}_{q,r}(t)(x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x)\wrt x = \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} \sum_{m=0}^\infty f^{\ell_0}_{m,q,r}(t)(x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x) \wrt x,\,  i\in\calS_q,\,j\in\calS_r\cup\calS_{r0},\]
%and 
%\[\int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} \mu^{\ell_0}_{q,r}(t)(\wrt x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x) \wrt x = \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} \sum_{m=0}^\infty \mu^{\ell_0}_{m,q,r}(t)(\wrt x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x) \wrt x,\,  i\in\calS_q,\,j\in\calS_r\cup\calS_{r0},\]
%\(q,r\in\{+,-\}\) and since the Laplace transform is a linear operator, then the Laplace transforms of (\ref{eqn: approx to sojourn}) and (\ref{eqn: trie thingy}) are
For \(q\in\{+,-,+0,-0\}\), \(r\in\{+.-\}\), consider the Laplace transforms 
\[\int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} \widehat f^{\ell_0}_{q,r}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x)\wrt x := \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} \sum_{m=0}^\infty \widehat f^{\ell_0}_{m,q,r}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x) \wrt x,\]
for \(i\in\calS_q,\,j\in\calS_r\cup\calS_{r0}\) and 
\[\int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} \widehat \mu^{\ell_0}_{q,r}(\lambda)( x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x) \wrt x := \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} \sum_{m=0}^\infty \widehat \mu^{\ell_0}_{m,q,r}(\lambda)( x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x) \wrt x,\]
for \(i\in\calS_q,\,j\in\calS_r\cup\calS_{r0}\)> 
The difference, 
\[\left|\int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} \widehat \mu^{\ell_0}_{q,r}(\lambda)( x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x)\wrt x  - \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} \widehat f^{\ell_0}_{q,r}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x) \wrt x \right|\] 
is less than or equal to 
\[\sum_{m=0}^\infty \left| \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} \widehat f^{\ell_0}_{m,q,r}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x)\wrt x - \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}}  \widehat \mu^{\ell_0}_{m,q,r}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x) \wrt x\right|,\]
which is an infinite sum of terms of the form of the left-hand side of (\ref{eqnALKJV}). The issue that remains is the that the bounds in Corollary~\ref{cor: k} are not necessarily summable (over \(m\)). In a step to resolving this issue, we have the following geometric domination condition. 
%Let \(\{Z\}_{p\in\mathbb N}\) be a sequence of matrix exponential random variables with \(\var\left(Z\right)\to 0\) as \(p\to \infty\). 
%
%\begin{cor}\label{cor: lst diff converge}
%	\begin{align*}
%                	& \widehat f^{\ell_0}_{m,+}(\lambda)(x,j_1,k_1,\dots,j_m,k_m,j; x_0,i) \to \widehat \mu^{\ell_0}_{m,+}(\lambda)(x,j_1,k_1,\dots,j_m,k_m,j; x_0,i)
%	\end{align*}
%	as \(p\to \infty\). 
%\end{cor}
%An analogous statement holds for 
%\[\widehat f^{\ell_0}_{m,-}(\lambda)(x,j_1,k_1,\dots,k_{m-1},j_m,j; x_0,i) \to \widehat \mu^{\ell_0}_{m,-}(\lambda)(x,j_1,k_1,\dots,k_{m-1},j_m,j; x_0,i)\]
%for \(m\geq 1\). 
%\begin{proof}
%	By Corollary~\ref{cor: lst diff converge}, the differences are bounded
%	\begin{align*}
%		&\left|\widehat f^{\ell_0}_{m,+}(\lambda)(x,j_1,k_1,\dots,j_m,k_m,j; x_0,i) - \widehat \mu^{\ell_0}_{m,+}(\lambda)(x,j_1,k_1,\dots,j_m,k_m,j; x_0,i)\right| 
%		%
%		\\&\leq R_m = \begin{cases}
%			|r_2| & m = 0, \\
%			|r_4| + |r_5| + m|r_4|  &  m\geq 1.
%			\end{cases} 
%	\end{align*}
%	By choosing \(\varepsilon = \var\left(Z\right)^{1/3}\), then \(|r_4|,\,|r_2|,\, |r_4|,\, |r_5|\) are all \(O\left(\var\left(Z\right)^{1/3}\right)\), and hence tend to \(0\) as \(p\to \infty\). 
%\end{proof}

Let \(c_{min} = \min\limits_{i\in\mathcal S_{+}\cup\calS_-} |c_i|\).
\begin{lem}\label{lem: gkjljklgagjklagsjlk}For all \(M\geq 0\), \(x\in\calD_{\ell_0,j}\), \(x_0\in\calD_{\ell_0,i}\), \(\ell_0\in\mathcal K, \ell_0\notin\{-1,K+1\}\), \(\lambda > 0\), \(q\in\{+,-,+0,-0\}\), \(r\in\{+,-\}\), \(i\in\calS\), \(j\in\calS_r\cup\calS_{r0}\),
	\begin{align}
		\sum_{m=M+1}^\infty \left| \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} \widehat f^{\ell_0}_{m,q,r}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x)\wrt x
		-
		\int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} \widehat \mu^{\ell_0}_{m,q,r}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x) \wrt x\right| \leq r_7^M
	\end{align}
	where 
	\[r_7^M =  \Delta FG(1+G_V)\left(\frac{q}{q+\lambda}\right)^{2M+2} \left(1-\left(\frac{q}{q+\lambda}\right)^2\right)^{-1} .\]
\end{lem}
Note that the bound \(r_7^M\) is independent of \(p\). 

We prove the result for \(q=r=+\) only, with the proof for the other cases following analogously. Essentially, this result follows from noting the probabilistic interpretation of the Laplace transforms \(\widehat f^{\ell_0}_{m,+,+}(t)(x,j;x_0,i)\), as the probability that, 
\begin{itemize}
	\item there are \(m\) changes from \(\mathcal S_+\) to \(\mathcal S_-\) and \(\calS_-\) to \(\calS_+\), 
	\item the orbit process \(\{\bs A(t)\}\) evolves accordingly, 
	\item and an exponential random variable with rate \(\lambda\) has not yet occurred.
\end{itemize}
We obtain an upper bound by ignoring the behaviour of the orbit process \(\{\bs A(t)\}\), then, by a uniformisation argument, we bound the probability that there are \(m\) changes from \(\mathcal S_+\) to \(\mathcal S_-\) and \(\calS_-\) to \(\calS_+\) before an exponential random variable with rate \(\lambda\) occurs, by the event that there are \(m\) independent exponential events before an exponential random variable with rate \(\lambda\) occurs.

Similarly, the probabilistic interpretation of the Laplace transforms \(\widehat \mu^{\ell_0}_{m,+,+}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i)\), as the probability that, 
\begin{itemize}
	\item there are \(m\) changes from \(\mathcal S_+\) to \(\mathcal S_-\) and \(\calS_-\) to \(\calS_+\), 
	\item the fluid level \(X(t)\) remains in \(\mathcal D_{\ell_0}\), 
	\item and an exponential random variable with rate \(\lambda\) has not yet occurred.
\end{itemize}
We obtain an upper bound by removing the requirement that the fluid level \(X(t)\) remain in \(\mathcal D_{\ell_0}\), then applying the same uniformisation argument as we do for \(\widehat f^{\ell_0}_{m,+,+}(t)(x,j;x_0,i)\).

\begin{proof}
	Consider \(i\in\calS_+,j\in\mathcal S_+\cup\calS_{+0}\). 
	By the triangle inequality, 
	\begin{align*}
		&\sum_{m=M+1}^\infty \left| \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} \widehat f^{\ell_0}_{m,+,+}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x) \wrt x
		-
		 \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} \widehat \mu^{\ell_0}_{m,+,+}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i) \psi(x) \wrt x \right|
		\\&\leq\sum_{m=M+1}^\infty \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} \widehat f^{\ell_0}_{m,+,+}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i) |\psi(x)| \wrt x
		\\&\qquad{} +\sum_{m=M+1}^\infty \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} \widehat  \mu^{\ell_0}_{m,+,+}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i) |\psi(x)| \wrt x,
	\end{align*}
	since all terms are non-negative. 
	
	Consider \(\widehat f^{\ell_0}_{m,+,+}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i) \), which is given by the \((i,j)\)th entry of
        \begin{align}
%        		&\sum_{j_1\in\mathcal S_-} \sum_{k_1\in\mathcal S_+}\dots \sum_{j_m\in\mathcal S_-}\sum_{k_m\in\mathcal S_+} \int_{x_1=0}^\infty h^{+-}_{i,j_{1}}(\lambda,x_1)\bs   a_{\ell_0,i}(x_0)e^{\bs{S}x_1}\wrt x_1 \bs{D}\nonumber
%	\int_{x_2=0}^\infty h^{-+}_{j_1,j_2}(\lambda,x_2) e^{\bs{S}x_2} \wrt x_2 \bs{D} 
%	\\&\hdots \int_{x_m=0}^\infty h^{-+}_{j_{m-1},j_m}(\lambda, x_m) e^{\bs{S}x_m} \wrt x_m \bs{D}
%	\int_{x_{m+1}=0}^\infty h^{++}_{j_m,j}(\lambda,x_{m+1}) e^{\bs{S}x_{m+1}}U_+(y_{\ell_0+1}-x) \wrt x_{m+1}\nonumber
%		%
%	&\int_{x_1=0}^\infty \bs H^{+-}(\lambda,x_1)\bs   a_{\ell_0,i}(x_0)e^{\bs{S}x_1}\wrt x_1 \bs{D}\nonumber
%	\int_{x_2=0}^\infty \bs H^{-+}(\lambda,x_2) e^{\bs{S}x_2} \wrt x_2 \bs{D} 
%	\int_{x_m=0}^\infty \bs H^{-+}(\lambda, x_m) e^{\bs{S}x_m} \wrt x_m \bs{D}
%	\\&\quad\hdots\int_{x_{m+1}=0}^\infty \bs H^{++}(\lambda,x_{m+1}) e^{\bs{S}x_{m+1}}U_+(y_{\ell_0+1}-x) \wrt x_{m+1}\nonumber
		%
%	\\&=\sum_{j_1\in\mathcal S_-} \sum_{k_1\in\mathcal S_+}\dots \sum_{j_m\in\mathcal S_-}\sum_{k_m\in\mathcal S_+} \int_{x_1=0}^\infty h^{+-}_{i,j_{1}}(\lambda,x_1)\nonumber
%	\int_{x_2=0}^\infty h^{-+}_{j_1,j_2}(\lambda,x_2) 
%	\hdots \int_{x_m=0}^\infty h^{-+}_{j_{m-1},j_m}(\lambda, x_m) 
%	\\&\int_{x_{m+1}=0}^\infty h^{++}_{j_m,j}(\lambda,x_{m+1}) \bs   a_{\ell_0,i}(x_0)e^{\bs{S}x_1}\wrt x_1 \bs{D}e^{\bs{S}x_2} \wrt x_2 \bs{D}\dots e^{\bs{S}x_m} \wrt x_m \bs{D}e^{\bs{S}x_{m+1}}U_+(y_{\ell_0+1}-x) \wrt x_{m+1}. \label{eqn:llkjhslkj}
	&\int_{x_1=0}^\infty \bs H^{+-}(\lambda,x_1)\nonumber
	\int_{x_2=0}^\infty \bs H^{-+}(\lambda,x_2) 
	\hdots \int_{x_m=0}^\infty \bs H^{-+}(\lambda, x_m) 
	\int_{x_{m+1}=0}^\infty \bs H^{++}(\lambda,x_{m+1}) 
	\\&\quad\bs   a_{\ell_0,i}(x_0)e^{\bs{S}x_1}\wrt x_1 \bs{D}e^{\bs{S}x_2} \wrt x_2 \bs{D}\dots e^{\bs{S}x_m} \wrt x_m \bs{D}e^{\bs{S}x_{m+1}}V(y_{\ell_0+1}-x) \wrt x_{m+1}. \label{eqn:llkjhslkj}
\end{align}
	Substituting the upper bound \(h^{++}_{j_m,j}(\lambda,x_{m+1})\leq G\), then (\ref{eqn:llkjhslkj}) is less than or equal to 
	\begin{align}
%		&\sum_{j_1\in\mathcal S_-} \sum_{k_1\in\mathcal S_+}\dots \sum_{j_m\in\mathcal S_-}\sum_{k_m\in\mathcal S_+} \int_{x_1=0}^\infty h^{+-}_{i,j_{1}}(\lambda,x_1)\nonumber
%	\int_{x_2=0}^\infty h^{-+}_{j_1,j_2}(\lambda,x_2) 
%	\hdots \int_{x_m=0}^\infty h^{-+}_{j_{m-1},j_m}(\lambda, x_m) 
%	\\&\int_{x_{m+1}=0}^\infty \bs   a_{\ell_0,i}(x_0)e^{\bs{S}x_1}\wrt x_1 \bs{D}e^{\bs{S}x_2} \wrt x_2 \bs{D}\dots e^{\bs{S}x_m} \wrt x_m \bs{D}e^{\bs{S}x_{m+1}}U_+(y_{\ell_0+1}-x)\wrt x_{m+1},
	&\int_{x_1=0}^\infty \bs H^{+-}(\lambda,x_1)\nonumber
	\int_{x_2=0}^\infty \bs H^{-+}(\lambda,x_2) 
	\hdots \int_{x_m=0}^\infty \bs H^{-+}(\lambda, x_m) \bs eG
	\\&\quad\int_{x_{m+1}=0}^\infty \bs   a_{\ell_0,i}(x_0)e^{\bs{S}x_1}\wrt x_1 \bs{D}e^{\bs{S}x_2} \wrt x_2 \bs{D}\dots e^{\bs{S}x_m} \wrt x_m \bs{D}e^{\bs{S}x_{m+1}}V(y_{\ell_0+1}-x)\wrt x_{m+1} \nonumber
	%
%	\\&=\sum_{j_1\in\mathcal S_-} \sum_{k_1\in\mathcal S_+}\dots \sum_{j_m\in\mathcal S_-}\sum_{k_m\in\mathcal S_+} \int_{x_1=0}^\infty h^{+-}_{i,j_{1}}(\lambda,x_1)\nonumber
%	\int_{x_2=0}^\infty h^{-+}_{j_1,j_2}(\lambda,x_2) 
%	\hdots \int_{x_m=0}^\infty h^{-+}_{j_{m-1},j_m}(\lambda, x_m) 
%	\\&\bs   a_{\ell_0,i}(x_0)e^{\bs{S}x_1}\wrt x_1 \bs{D}e^{\bs{S}x_2} \wrt x_2 \bs{D}\dots e^{\bs{S}x_m} \wrt x_m \bs{D}(-\bs S)^{-1}U_+(y_{\ell_0+1}-x),
	\\&=\int_{x_1=0}^\infty \bs H^{+-}(\lambda,x_1)\nonumber
	\int_{x_2=0}^\infty \bs H^{-+}(\lambda,x_2) 
	\hdots \int_{x_m=0}^\infty \bs H^{-+}(\lambda, x_m) \bs eG
	\\&\quad \bs   a_{\ell_0,i}(x_0)e^{\bs{S}x_1}\wrt x_1 \bs{D}e^{\bs{S}x_2} \wrt x_2 \bs{D}\dots e^{\bs{S}x_m} \wrt x_m \bs{D}(-\bs{S})^{-1}V(y_{\ell_0+1}-x) \nonumber
	% 
%	\\&\leq\sum_{j_1\in\mathcal S_-} \sum_{k_1\in\mathcal S_+}\dots \sum_{j_m\in\mathcal S_-}\sum_{k_m\in\mathcal S_+} \int_{x_1=0}^\infty h^{+-}_{i,j_{1}}(\lambda,x_1)\nonumber
%	\int_{x_2=0}^\infty h^{-+}_{j_1,j_2}(\lambda,x_2) 
%	\hdots \int_{x_m=0}^\infty h^{-+}_{j_{m-1},j_m}(\lambda, x_m) 
%	\\&\quad\bs   a_{\ell_0,i}(x_0)e^{\bs{S}x_1}\wrt x_1 \bs{D}e^{\bs{S}x_2} \wrt x_2 \bs{D}\dots e^{\bs{S}x_m} \wrt x_m \bs eH, \label{eqn: this 12}
	\\&\leq\int_{x_1=0}^\infty \bs H^{+-} (\lambda,x_1)\nonumber
	\int_{x_2=0}^\infty \bs H^{-+} (\lambda,x_2) 
	\hdots \int_{x_m=0}^\infty \bs H^{-+} (\lambda, x_m) \bs eG
	\\&\quad\bs   a_{\ell_0,i}(x_0)e^{\bs{S}x_1}\wrt x_1 \bs{D}e^{\bs{S}x_2} \wrt x_2 \bs{D}\dots e^{\bs{S}x_m} \wrt x_m \bs eG_V, \label{eqn: this 12}	
        \end{align}
        The last inequality holds since 
        \[\bs D(-\bs S)^{-1}V(x) = \int_{u=0}^\infty e^{\bs Su}\bs s\cfrac{\bs \alpha e^{\bs S u}}{\bs \alpha e^{\bs S u}\bs e}(-\bs S)^{-1}V(x)\wrt u \leq \int_{u=0}^\infty e^{\bs Su}\bs s\cfrac{\bs \alpha e^{\bs S u}\bs e}{\bs \alpha e^{\bs S u}\bs e}G_V = \bs eG_V,\]
        which relies on Property \ref{properties: 1}. 
        
	Now, applying Lamma \ref{lem:macmnm} repeatedly gives the bound  
	\[\bs   a_{\ell_0,i}(x_0)e^{\bs{S}x_1}\bs{D}e^{\bs{S}x_2} \bs{D}\dots e^{\bs{S}x_m} \bs e \leq 1.\]
%	This bound could also have been obtained by observing that \(\bs   a_{\ell_0,i}(x_0)e^{\bs{S}x_1}\bs{D}e^{\bs{S}x_2} \bs{D}\dots e^{\bs{S}x_m} \bs e \) is a probability. 

	Hence (\ref{eqn: this 12}) is less than or equal to 
	\begin{align}
%		& \sum_{j_1\in\mathcal S_-} \sum_{k_1\in\mathcal S_+}\dots \sum_{j_m\in\mathcal S_-}\sum_{k_m\in\mathcal S_+} \int_{x_1=0}^\infty h^{+-}_{i,j_{1}}(\lambda,x_1) \wrt x_1 \int_{x_2=0}^\infty h^{-+}_{j_1,k_1}(\lambda,x_2)  \wrt x_2  
%                	\hdots \int_{x_{2m}=0}^\infty h^{-+}_{j_{m},k_m}(\lambda, x_{2m})\wrt x_{2m}H \label{eqn: this 123}
		& \int_{x_1=0}^\infty \bs H^{+-}(\lambda,x_1) \wrt x_1 \int_{x_2=0}^\infty \bs H^{-+}(\lambda,x_2)  \wrt x_2  
                	\hdots \int_{x_{2m}=0}^\infty \bs H^{-+}(\lambda, x_{2m})\wrt x_{2m}\bs e G_VG. \label{eqn: this 123}
        \end{align}
	        
        The stochastic interpretation of the \(i\)th element of the vector \(\bs H^{+-}(\lambda,x)\bs e\) is that it is the probability density that the phase of the fluid queue changes from a positive to a negative phase at the time when the in-out fluid has increased by \(\wrt x\) and before an exponential random variable with rate \(\lambda\) occurs, given the phase is initially \(i\). There may be multiple changes of phase within \(\mathcal S_+\cup\calS_{+0}\) before the first change from \(\mathcal \mathcal S_+\cup\calS_{+0}\) to \(\mathcal S_-\). The first change of phase occurs at rate (with respect to the in-out level) \(-T_{ii}/|c_i|\) and this is the lowest in-out fluid level at which it may be possible for us to see a transition from \(\mathcal S_+\) to \(\mathcal S_-\). Consider a uniformisation of the phase process of the in-out fluid with uniformisation parameter \(q = \max\limits_{i\in\mathcal S}-T_{ii}/|c_i|\). Then the first event of the uniformised phase process occurs at rate \(q\) and occurs at, or before, the first change of phase. Hence the first uniformisation event occurs at, or before the first change from \(\mathcal S_+\cup\calS_{+0}\) to \(\mathcal S_-\). This gives the bound \(\bs H^{+-}(\lambda,x)\bs e\leq qe^{-(\lambda + q)x}\bs e\).
        
        Similarly for \(\bs H^{-+}(\lambda,x)\bs e\leq qe^{-(\lambda + q)x}\bs e\).
        
        From this stochastic interpretation, (\ref{eqn: this 123}) is less than or equal to 
        \begin{align}
%		& \sum_{j_1\in\mathcal S_-} \sum_{k_1\in\mathcal S_+}\dots \sum_{j_m\in\mathcal S_-}\sum_{k_m\in\mathcal S_+} \int_{x_1=0}^\infty h^{+-}_{i,j_{1}}(\lambda,x_1) \wrt x_1 \int_{x_2=0}^\infty h^{-+}_{j_1,k_1}(\lambda,x_2)  \wrt x_2  
%                	\hdots \int_{x_{2m}=0}^\infty h^{-+}_{j_{m},k_m}(\lambda, x_{2m})\wrt x_{2m}H\label{eqn: gjfjelwl}
%		%
%		\\&\leq \sum_{j_1\in\mathcal S_-} \sum_{k_1\in\mathcal S_+}\dots \sum_{j_m\in\mathcal S_-} \int_{x_1=0}^\infty h^{+-}_{i,j_{1}}(\lambda,x_1) \wrt x_1 \int_{x_2=0}^\infty h^{-+}_{j_1,k_1}(\lambda,x_2)  \wrt x_2  
%                	\hdots \int_{x_m=0}^\infty qe^{(-q-\lambda)x_m}\wrt x_{2m}H \nonumber
%		%
%		\\&\leq \int_{x_1=0}^\infty qe^{(-q-\lambda)x_1}  \wrt x_1 \int_{x_2=0}^\infty qe^{(-q-\lambda)x_2}  \wrt x_2  
%                	\hdots \int_{x_{2m}=0}^\infty qe^{(-q-\lambda)x_{2m}}\wrt x_{2m}H \nonumber
%		%
%		\\&= \left(\cfrac{q}{q+\lambda}\right)^{2m}H\nonumber
%		& \int_{x_1=0}^\infty \bs H^{+-}(\lambda,x_1) \wrt x_1 \int_{x_2=0}^\infty \bs H^{-+}(\lambda,x_2)  \bs e\wrt x_2  
%                	\hdots \int_{x_{2m}=0}^\infty qe^{-1 x_{2m}}\bs e\wrt x_{2m}H\label{eqn: gjfjelwl}
		%
		&\bs H^{+-}(\lambda,x_1) \wrt x_1 \int_{x_2=0}^\infty \bs H^{-+}(\lambda,x_2)  \wrt x_2  
                	\hdots \int_{x_m=0}^\infty qe^{(-q-\lambda)x_m}\wrt x_{2m}G_VG \nonumber
		%
		\\&\leq \bs e\int_{x_1=0}^\infty qe^{(-q-\lambda)x_1}  \wrt x_1 \int_{x_2=0}^\infty qe^{(-q-\lambda)x_2}  \wrt x_2  
                	\hdots \int_{x_{2m}=0}^\infty qe^{(-q-\lambda)x_{2m}}\wrt x_{2m}G_VG \nonumber
		%
		\\&= \bs e\left(\cfrac{q}{q+\lambda}\right)^{2m}G_VG.\label{eqn: bound ggggaaaa}
        \end{align}
        Hence,  
        \begin{align}
	         &\sum_{m=M+1}^\infty \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} \widehat f^{\ell_0}_{m,+,+}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i)|\psi(x)|\wrt x \nonumber
	        \\&\leq  {G_V}G  \sum_{m=M+1}^\infty \left(\cfrac{q}{q+\lambda}\right)^{2m}\int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} |\psi(x)|\wrt x \nonumber
	        \\&\leq {G_V}G \left(\cfrac{q}{q+\lambda}\right)^{2M+2} \left(1-\left(\cfrac{q}{q+\lambda}\right)^2\right)^{-1} \Delta F.
        \end{align}
        
        Now consider \(\widehat\mu_{m,+,+}^{\ell_0}(\lambda)( x,j;x_0,i) \) which is given by the \((i,j)\)th entry of 
        \begin{align}
		\nonumber& \int_{x_1 = 0}^{\Delta-(x_0-y_{\ell_0})} \bs H^{+-}(\lambda,\Delta-(x_0-y_{\ell_0})-x_1) \int_{x_2 = 0}^{\Delta-x_1} \bs H^{-+}(\lambda,\Delta - x_2-x_1) \wrt x_1 
		\\\nonumber &\quad\dots  
		\int_{x_{2m}=0}^{\Delta-x_{m-1}} \bs H^{-+}(\lambda,\Delta -x_{2m-1} - x_{2m}) \wrt x_{2m-1}
		 \bs H^{++}(\lambda,\Delta -x_{2m}- (y_{\ell_0+1}- x))\wrt x_{2m}
		\\\nonumber&= \int_{x_1 = (x_0-y_{\ell_0})}^{\Delta} \bs H^{+-}(\lambda,\Delta-x_1) \int_{x_2 = x_1}^{\Delta} \bs H^{-+}(\lambda,\Delta -x_2) \wrt x_1 
		\dots  
		\\&\int_{x_{2m}=x_{2m-1}}^{\Delta} \bs H^{-+}(\lambda,\Delta - x_{2m}) \wrt x_{2m-1}
		\bs H^{++}(\lambda,\Delta -x_{2m}-x_{2m-1}- (y_{\ell_0+1}- x))\nonumber 
		\\&\qquad {}\wrt x_{2m-1}\wrt x_{2m}.\label{eqn:m789J}
        \end{align}
        Once again, use the bound \(h^{++}_{j_m,j}(\lambda,x_{m+1})\leq G\). Hence (\ref{eqn:m789J}) is less than or equal to 
        \begin{align}
        		&\int_{x_1 = (x_0-y_{\ell_0})}^{\Delta} \bs H^{+-}(\lambda,\Delta-x_1) \int_{x_2 = x_1}^{\Delta} \bs H^{-+}(\lambda,\Delta -x_2) \wrt x_1 \nonumber
		\\&\quad\dots  
		\int_{x_{2m}=x_{2m-1}}^{\Delta} \bs H^{-+}(\lambda,\Delta - x_{2m}) \wrt x_{2m-1}
		\wrt x_{2m-1}\wrt x_{2m}G.\label{eqn:m789J2}
        \end{align}
        The expression (\ref{eqn:m789J2}) differs from (\ref{eqn: this 123}) only by a constant factor \(G_V\) and that the integrals in the former are finite, hence we may bound it in the same way as (\ref{eqn: this 123}). Therefore, 
%        Since \(h_{j_mj}^{--}(\lambda,\Delta -x_{m}- (x-y_{\ell_0}))\leq 1\) as it is a probability. 
%	Using the same uniformisation argument, this is bounded by 
%	\begin{align}
%		& \int_{x_1 = 0}^{\Delta-(x_0-y_{\ell_0})} qe^{(-q-\lambda)(\Delta-(x_0-y_{\ell_0})-x_1)}
%		\int_{x_2 = 0}^{\Delta-x_1}qe^{(-q-\lambda)(\Delta -x_1- x_2)} \wrt x_1 \dots 
%		\int_{x_{m}=0}^{\Delta-x_{m-1}} qe^{(-q-\lambda)(\Delta-x_{m-1} - x_{m})} \wrt x_{m-1}
%		\wrt x_m
%		%
%		\\&= \int_{x_1 = x_0-y_{\ell_0}}^{\Delta} qe^{(-q-\lambda)(\Delta-x_1)}
%		\int_{x_2 = x_1}^{\Delta}qe^{(-q-\lambda)(\Delta - x_2)} \wrt x_1 \dots 
%		\int_{x_{m}=x_{m-1}}^{\Delta} qe^{(-q-\lambda)(\Delta-x_{m})} \wrt x_{m-1}
%		\wrt x_m
%		% 
%		\\&\leq \int_{x_1 = 0}^{\Delta} qe^{(-q-\lambda)(\Delta-x_1)}
%		\int_{x_2 = 0}^{\Delta}qe^{(-q-\lambda)(\Delta - x_2)} \wrt x_1 \dots 
%		\int_{x_{m}=0}^{\Delta} qe^{(-q-\lambda)(\Delta-x_{m})} \wrt x_{m-1}
%		\wrt x_m
%		%
%		\\&= \left(\cfrac{q}{q+\lambda}\left(1-e^{(-q-\lambda)\Delta}\right)\right)^m.
%        \end{align}
%        Similarly for \(\widehat\mu_{m,-}^{\ell_0}(\lambda)(\wrt x,j;x_0,i) \) we can show it is bounded by 
%        \[\left(\cfrac{q}{q+\lambda}\left(1-e^{(-q-\lambda)\Delta}\right)\right)^{m-1}.\]
        
%        Returning to the limit of the tail-sum of \(\widehat \mu_{m,+}^{\ell_0}\) in the last line of (\ref{eqn: geom sum}), we can now bound it by 
        \begin{align}
	         & \sum_{m=M+1}^\infty \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} |\psi(x)|\wrt x \widehat \mu^{\ell_0}_{m,+,+}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i) |\psi(x)|\wrt x \nonumber
	        \\&\leq G\left(\cfrac{q}{q+\lambda}\right)^{2M+2} \left(1-\left(\cfrac{q}{q+\lambda}\right)^2\right)^{-1}\Delta F.
        \end{align}
        
	Analogous arguments show the same bounds for any \(i,j\in\mathcal S\). 
\end{proof}

\begin{lem} \label{lem:vn4}
	For all \(x\in\calD_{\ell_0,j}\), \(x_0\in\calD_{\ell_0,i}\), \(i,j\in\calS\), \(\ell_0\in\mathcal K, \ell_0\notin\{-1,K+1\}\), \(\lambda > 0\),  
	\begin{align}
		&\left|\int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}}\widehat f^{\ell_0}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x) \wrt x - \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}}\widehat \mu^{\ell_0}(\lambda)( x,j; x_0,i)\psi(x) \wrt x\right|\to 0  \label{eqn: akhv}
%		\leq R(i,j,M).
	\end{align}
	as \(p\to\infty\). 
%	where 
%	\begin{align*}
%			R(i,j,M) &= R_{V,2} GF + \varepsilon GF + \sum_{m=1}^{M} |r_9(2m)||\calS_+|^m|\calS_-|^m + r_7^M, \intertext{for \(i\in\calS_+,\,j\in\calS_{+}\cup\calS_{+0},\mbox{ or } i\in\calS_-,j\in\calS_{-}\cup\calS_{-0},\)}
%			R(i,j,M) &=\sum_{m=0}^{M} |r_9(2m+1)||\calS_+|^{m+1}|\calS_-|^m + r_7^M, 
%			\intertext{for \(i\in\calS_-,\,j\in\calS_{+}\cup\calS_{+0},\)}
%			R(i,j,M) &=\sum_{m=0}^{M} |r_9(2m+1)||\calS_+|^{m}|\calS_-|^{m+1} + r_7^M, 
%			\intertext{for \( i\in\calS_+,j\in\calS_{-}\cup\calS_{-0},\)}
%			R(i,j,M) &= |r_{10}| +\sum_{m=1}^{M} |r_9(2m)||\calS_+|^{m}|\calS_-|^{m+1} \nonumber
%			\\&\qquad{}+(|r_9(2m+1)|+|r_8(2m+1)|\Delta F)|\calS_+|^{m+1}|\calS_-|^{m+1} + r_7^M, 
%			\intertext{for \(i\in\calS_{0+},j\in\mathcal S_+,\)}
%			R(i,j,M) &=\sum_{m=0}^{M} |r_9(2m+1)||\calS_+|^{m+1}|\calS_-|^{m+1} + (|r_9(2m)|+|r_8(2m)|\Delta F)|\calS_+|^{m}|\calS_-|^{m+1} + r_7^M, 
%			\intertext{for \(i\in\calS_{0-},j\in\mathcal S_+,\)}
%			R(i,j,M) &=\sum_{m=0}^{M} |r_9(2m+1)||\calS_+|^{m+1}|\calS_-|^{m+1} + (|r_9(2m)|+|r_8(2m)|\Delta F)|\calS_+|^{m+1}|\calS_-|^{m} + r_7^M, 
%			\intertext{for \(i\in\calS_{0+},j\in\mathcal S_-,\)}
%			R(i,j,M) &= |r_{10}| + \sum_{m=1}^{M} |r_9(2m)||\calS_+|^{m}|\calS_-|^{m+1} \nonumber 
%			\\&\qquad{}+(|r_9(2m+1)|+|r_8(2m+1)|\Delta F)|\calS_+|^{m+1}|\calS_-|^{m+1} + r_7^M,
%			\intertext{for \(i\in\calS_{0-},j\in\mathcal S_-.\)}
%	\end{align*}
\end{lem}
\begin{proof}
	 
	
	Consider \(i\in\calS_+\) and \(j\in\calS_+\cup\calS_{+0}\). By partitioning on the number of changes from \(\calS_-\to\calS_+\), (\ref{eqn: akhv}) can be written as
	\begin{align}
%		&\nonumber\left| \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}}\widehat f^{\ell_0}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x)\wrt x -  \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}}\widehat \mu^{\ell_0}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x) \wrt x\right| 
%		%&=
		&\left|\sum_{m=0}^\infty \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}}\widehat f^{\ell_0}_{m,+,+}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x)\wrt x
		-
		\sum_{m=0}^\infty \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} \widehat \mu^{\ell_0}_{m,+,+}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x)\wrt x\right| \nonumber
		\\&\leq \sum_{m=0}^\infty \left| \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}}\widehat f^{\ell_0}_{m,+,+}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x)\wrt x
		-
		\int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} \widehat \mu^{\ell_0}_{m,+,+}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x)\wrt x\right|. \label{eqn:ASLKF}
%		\\&\leq \sum_{m=0}^M \left| \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} \widehat f^{\ell_0}_{m,+,+}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x)\wrt x
%		-
%		\int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} \widehat \mu^{\ell_0}_{m,+,+}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x)\wrt x\right|\nonumber 
%		\\&\quad{}+ \sum_{m=M+1}^\infty \left| \int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} \widehat f^{\ell_0}_{m,+,+}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x) \wrt x
%		-
%		\int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} \widehat \mu^{\ell_0}_{m,+,+}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x)\wrt x\right|\label{eqn: kajklgaajklgkjlag}
%	\end{align}
%	By Corollary~\ref{cor: k} we have the bound 
%        \begin{align}
%        		&\sum_{m=0}^M \left| \widehat f^{\ell_0}_{m,+,+}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i) \nonumber 
%		-
%		\int_{x\in\calD_{\ell_0}} \widehat \mu^{\ell_0}_{m,+,+}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i)\psi(x) \wrt x\right|
%		\\&\leq R_{V,2} GF + \varepsilon GF + \sum_{m=1}^M (|r_9(2m)| |\calS_+|^m|\calS_-|^m). \label{eqn: aklfj9390skdl}
        \end{align}
        By Corollary \ref{cor: k} each term in the sum (\ref{eqn:ASLKF}) converges to \(0\) as \(p\to\infty\). Lemma~\ref{lem: gkjljklgagjklagsjlk} gives a domination condition, so we can apply the Dominated Convergence Theorem which proves the stated convergence in (\ref{eqn: akhv}).
        
        Analogous arguments can be applied for any \(i,j\in\mathcal S\). 
%        The bound (\ref{eqn: aklfj9390skdl}), together with the bounds on the tail sums in Lemma~\ref{lem: gkjljklgagjklagsjlk}, gives a bound for (\ref{eqn: kajklgaajklgkjlag}), and this completes the proof for \(i\in\calS_+\) and \(j\in\calS_+\cup\calS_{+0}\). The proofs for the other cases follow analogous arguments. 
\end{proof}

%Given and \(\delta>0\) we can find an \(M\) such that \(r_7^M\leq \delta/2\), and then find a \(p_0\) sufficiently large so that, for all \(p\geq p_0\), the error bounds in Lemma~\ref{lem:vn4} are less than \(\delta\), thereby showing convergence of \(\widehat f^{\ell_0}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i) \) to \(\widehat \mu^{\ell_0}(\lambda)( x,j; x_0,i)\).

\begin{rem}\label{rem: point wies}
	For a fixed \(\lambda > 0\), convergence of 
	\begin{align}
		\left|\widehat f^{\ell_0}(\lambda)(x,j;x_0,i) - \widehat \mu^{\ell_0}(\lambda)( x,j; x_0,i) \right|
	\end{align}
	actually holds point-wise for each \(\ell_0\in\mathcal K\setminus\{-1,K+1\}\), and each \(i,j\in\mathcal S,\) \(x_0\in\mathcal D_{\ell_0,i}\), \(x\in\calD_{\ell_0,j}\) except at the set of points where \(x=x_0\). Specifically, the lack of point-wise convergence at this point occurs due terms with the index \(m=0\), that is, terms where there are no changes of phase from \(\calS_+\to\calS_-\) or \(\calS_-\to \calS_+\). On these sample paths the relevant Laplace transforms of the fluid queue are discontinuous at this point. For example, 
	\begin{align*}
		\widehat \mu^{\ell_0}_{0,+,+}(\lambda)( x,j;x_0,i) \wrt x&= h_{ij}^{++}(\lambda,x-x_0)1(x\geq x_0)\wrt x,
	\end{align*}
	is discontinuous at \(x=x_0\). If we were to insist on point-wise convergence, then we would need to enforce the error term \(r_V(u,v)\to 0\) point-wise for each \(u,v\). In the cases presented here \(r_V(u,v)\) converges point-wise to 0 everywhere except \(u+v=\Delta\). 
\end{rem}

\subsection{Convergence at changes of level} Before moving on to global convergence we need another result about convergence of the QBD-RAP scheme and the fluid queue at changes of level. 

Let \(E^\lambda\) be an exponential random variable with rate \(\lambda\). In the following we use the stochastic interpretation of the Laplace transform of a probability distribution with non-negative support: for a random variable \(W\) with distribution function \(F_W(w)= \mathbb P(W<w)\), then \(\displaystyle\int_{w=0}^\infty e^{-\lambda w} \wrt F_W(w) = \mathbb P(W < E^{\lambda})\). That is, the Laplace transform with parameter \(\lambda >0\) is the probability that \(W\) occurs before an exponential time with rate \(\lambda\) occurs. 

Regarding Remark \ref{rem: point wies} we do require convergence at certain boundary points which correspond to changes of level of the QBD-RAP. To this end, we have to following result. 
\begin{cor}\label{cor: aln222} For \(\ell,\ell_0\in \mathcal K \setminus \{-1,K+1\},\) \(x_0\in\mathcal D_{\ell_0,i}\), \(i\in\mathcal S\)
	then, for \(j\in\calS_+\),
	\begin{align}
		&\mathbb P(L(\tau_1) = \ell_0+1, \varphi(\tau_1) = j, \tau_{1}\leq E^\lambda 
            	 \mid L(0) = \ell_{0},\bs A(0)=\bs  a_{\ell_0,i}(x_0), \varphi(0) = i) \nonumber
	 	%
		\\&\to \mathbb P(X(\tau_1^X) = y_{\ell_0+1}, \varphi(\tau_1^X) = j, \tau_{1}^X\leq E^\lambda 
            	 \mid X(0) = x_0, \varphi(0) = i)\label{eqn: 1421}
		%
%		 \\&\leq \begin{cases}
%			|r_2| + \sum_{m=1}^{M} |r_9(2m)||\calS_+|^m|\calS_-|^m + r_7^M, &i\in\calS_+,\,j\in\calS_{+} ,
%			\\ \sum_{m=0}^{M} |r_9(2m+1)||\calS_+|^{m+1}|\calS_-|^m + r_7^M, &i\in\calS_-,\,j\in\calS_{+},
%			\\ \sum_{m=0}^{M} |r_9(2m+1)||\calS_+|^{m+1}|\calS_-|^{m+1} + (|r_9(2m)|+|r_8(2m)|\Delta F)|\calS_+|^{m}|\calS_-|^{m+1} + r_7^M, &i\in\calS_{0-},j\in\mathcal S_+,
%			\\ \sum_{m=0}^{M} |r_9(2m+1)||\calS_+|^{m+1}|\calS_-|^{m+1} + (|r_9(2m)|+|r_8(2m)|\Delta F)|\calS_+|^{m}|\calS_-|^{m+1} + r_7^M, &i\in\calS_{0-},j\in\mathcal S_+.
%			\end{cases}		\label{eqn: 1421} %
		 %
		 %
		 %
		 \intertext{and for \(j\in\calS_-\)}
		 &\mathbb P(L(\tau_1) = \ell_0-1, \varphi(\tau_1) = j, \tau_{1}\leq E^\lambda 
            	 \mid L(0) = \ell_{0},\bs A(0)=\bs  a_{\ell_0,i}(x_0), \varphi(0) = i) \nonumber
	 	%
		\\&\to \mathbb P(X(\tau_1^X) = y_{\ell_0}, \varphi(\tau_1^X) = j, \tau_{1}^X\leq E^\lambda 
            	 \mid X(0) = x_0, \varphi(0) = i). \nonumber
		%
%		 \\&\leq \begin{cases}
%			|r_2|  + \sum_{m=1}^{M} |r_9(2m)||\calS_+|^m|\calS_-|^m + r_7^M, & i\in\calS_-,j\in\calS_{-}\cup\calS_{-0},
%			\\ \sum_{m=0}^{M} |r_9(2m+1)||\calS_+|^{m}|\calS_-|^{m+1} + r_7^M, & i\in\calS_+,j\in\calS_{-}\cup\calS_{-0},
%			\\\sum_{m=0}^{M} |r_9(2m+1)||\calS_+|^{m+1}|\calS_-|^{m+1} + (|r_9(2m)|+|r_8(2m)|\Delta F)|\calS_+|^{m+1}|\calS_-|^{m} + r_7^M, &i\in\calS_{0+},j\in\mathcal S_-,
%			\\|r_{10}| + \sum_{m=1}^{M} |r_9(2m)||\calS_+|^{m}|\calS_-|^{m+1} + (|r_9(2m+1)|+|r_8(2m+1)|\Delta F)|\calS_+|^{m+1}|\calS_-|^{m+1} + r_7^M, &i\in\calS_{0-},j\in\mathcal S_-.
%			\end{cases}
	\end{align}
	At a boundary, for \(\ell_0\in\{-1,K+1\}\), 
	\begin{align}
		&\mathbb P(L(\tau_1) = \ell, \varphi(\tau_1) = j, \tau_{1}\leq E^\lambda 
            	 \mid L(0) = \ell_{0},\bs A(0)=1, \varphi(0) = i) \nonumber
	 	%
		\\&= \mathbb P(X(\tau_1^X) = x, \varphi(\tau_1^X) = j, \tau_{1}\leq E^\lambda 
            	 \mid X(0) = 0, \varphi(0) = i), \label{eqn: lk78GHJK}
	\end{align}
	where \(\ell = 0\), \(i\in\calS_-\cup\calS_{-0}\) and \(j\in\mathcal S_+\) if \(\ell_0=-1\), and \(\ell = K\), \(i\in\calS_+\cup\calS_{+0}\) and \(j\in\calS_-\) if \(\ell_0=K+1\).  
\end{cor}
\begin{proof}
	The proof follows the same structure as the proof of Lemma~\ref{lem:vn4} however changes are required in all the results used in the proof, as here we do not integrate a function \(\psi\). Here we only give and outline of the proof. 

	Consider first \(i\in \calS_+,j\in\calS_+\cup\calS_{+0}\). Partition the probability (\ref{eqn: 1421}) on the times \(\{\Sigma_n\}_{n\geq 1}\) and \(\{\Gamma_n\}_{n\geq 1}\), specifically, partition on the event that there are exactly \(m\) events \(\{\Sigma_n\}_{n=1}^m\) and exactly \(m\) events \(\{\Gamma_n\}_{n=1}^m\). Partition further by the phases at these times \(\varphi(\Sigma_n)=j_n\in\calS_-\), \(n=1,\dots,m\) and \(\varphi(\Gamma_n)=k_n\in\calS_+\), \(n=1,...,m\). The resulting partitioned probabilities are
	\begin{align}
                 &\int_{x_1=0}^\infty h^{+-}_{i,j_{1}}(\lambda,x_1)\bs   a_{\ell_0,i}(x_0)e^{\bs{S}x_1}\wrt x_1 \bs{D}\nonumber
            	\\&\nonumber \quad \left[\prod_{r=1}^{m-1} \int_{x_{2r}=0}^\infty h^{-+}_{j_r,k_r}(\lambda,x_{2r}) e^{\bs{S}x_{2r}}\wrt x_{2r}\bs D \int_{x_{2r+1}=0}^\infty h^{+-}_{k_rj_{r+1}}(\lambda,x_{2r+1}) e^{\bs{S}x_{2r+1}} \wrt x_{2r+1}\bs D\right]
            	\\&
            	\quad \int_{x_{2m}=0}^\infty h^{-+}_{j_{m},k_m}(\lambda, x_{2m}) e^{\bs{S}x_{2m}} \wrt x_{2m} \bs{D}\int_{x_{2m+1}=0}^\infty h^{++}_{k_m,j}(\lambda,x_{2m+1}) e^{\bs{S}x_{2m+1}}\wrt x_{2m+1}\bs s  \label{eqn: prob ofjaiv}
	\end{align}
	and (\ref{eqn: 1421}) is obtained by summing over \(j_1,\dots,j_m\), \(k_1,\dots,k_m\), \(m\geq 0\). 
	
	Corollary~\ref{cor: cond bnd} and Lemma~\ref{lem:tttttt} are analogous to Lemma~\ref{lem: Dcoajc} and Corollary~\ref{lem: Dcoajc} used in the proof of Lemma~\ref{lem:vn4}. They provide relevant bounds for the difference between terms like (\ref{eqn: prob ofjaiv}) for \(m=0\) and 
	\[\mathbb P(X(\tau_1^X)=y_{\ell_0+1},\varphi(\tau_1^X)=j,\tau_1^X\leq E^\lambda, \tau_1<\Sigma_1 \mid X(0)=x_0, \varphi(0)=i) = h_{ij}^{++}(\lambda,y_{\ell_0+1}-x_0),\]
	for example.
	
	Corollaries \ref{cor: a cor} and \ref{cor: aaaaa} are analogous to Corollaries \ref{eqn: lafkjebjcbbalbvvbrb} and \ref{cor: fljm7778} used in the proof of Lemma~\ref{lem:vn4}. Corollaries \ref{cor: a cor} and \ref{cor: aaaaa} give error bounds for the difference between terms such as (\ref{eqn: prob ofjaiv}) for \(m\geq 1\) and the corresponding probability for the fluid queue, 
	\begin{align}
		&\mathbb P(X(\tau_1^X)=y_{\ell_0+1},\varphi(\tau_1^X)=j,\tau_1^X\leq E^\lambda, \Sigma_{m}\leq \tau_1<\Gamma_{m+1}, \varphi(\Sigma_\ell) = j_\ell, \varphi(\Gamma_\ell)=k_\ell, \nonumber
		\\&\qquad{} \ell = 1,\dots, m  \mid X(0)=x_0, \varphi(0)=i)
	\end{align}
	which is given by (\ref{eqn: lst herwe}). 
	
	The error bounds on each term in the partition imply that all the terms converge to the corresponding terms for the fluid queue. Equation~(\ref{eqn: bound ggggaaaa}) provides a domination condition. Thus we can apply the Dominated Convergence Theorem to prove that the sum of the partitioned probabilities (\ref{eqn: prob ofjaiv}) converges as \(p\to\infty\). The sum of the limits is 
	\[\mathbb P(X(\tau_1^X) = y_{\ell_0+1}, \varphi(\tau_1^X) = j, \tau_{1}\leq E^\lambda 
            	 \mid X(0) = x_0, \varphi(0) = i).\]
	 
	 The result for all other cases \(i,j\in\calS\) follow analogously.
	
	At a boundary we can model the fluid queue exactly, hence (\ref{eqn: lk78GHJK}) holds.
	
%	The expresstion (\ref{eqn: prob ofjaiv}) is also obtained if we choose the closing operator to be \(V(x)=e^{\bs Sx}\bs s\) and evaluate Laplace transform with respect to time of the estimate of \(\bar X(t)=y_{\ell_0+1}\).
%	
%	
%	This is a specific case of Lemma~\ref{lem:vn4} where we choose the closing operator to be \(V(0) = \bs s\). 
	
%	The Laplace transform of the time taken for the QBD-RAP to change level on the event that it does so in phase \(j\in\mathcal S_+\), there are \(m\) changes of phase from \(\mathcal S_+\) to \(\mathcal S_-\) and \(m\) changes of phase from \(\mathcal S_-\) to \(\mathcal S_+\), and the phases immediately after these times are \(j_1,\dots,j_m\in\mathcal S_-\) and \(k_1,\dots,k_m\in\mathcal S_+\), respectively, given the initial phase is \(i\) and orbit position is \(\bs   a_{\ell_0,i}(x_0)\) is
%	\begin{align}
%	&\int_{x_1=0}^\infty h^{+-}_{i,j_{1}}(\lambda,x_1)\bs   a_{\ell_0,i}(x_0)e^{\bs{S}x_1}\wrt x_1 \bs{D}\nonumber
%	\int_{x_2=0}^\infty h^{-+}_{j_1,k_1}(\lambda,x_2) e^{\bs{S}x_2} \wrt x_2 \bs{D} 
%	\hdots \int_{x_{2m}=0}^\infty h^{-+}_{j_{m},k_m}(\lambda, x_{2m}) e^{\bs{S}x_{2m}} \wrt x_{2m} \bs{D}
%	\\&
%	\int_{x_{2m+1}=0}^\infty h^{++}_{k_m,j}(\lambda,x_{2m+1}) e^{\bs{S}x_{2m+1}}\wrt x_{2m+1}\bs s\wrt x/|c_j|. \label{eqn:m4sfkn}
%	\end{align}
%	The events that there are \(m\) changes of phase from \(\mathcal S_+\) to \(\mathcal S_-\) and \(m\) changes of phase from \(\mathcal S_-\) to \(\mathcal S_+\), and the phases immediately after these times are \(j_1,\dots,j_m\in\mathcal S_-\) and \(k_1,\dots,k_m\in\mathcal S_+\), respectively, form a partition for \[\mathbb P(L(\tau_1) = \ell, \varphi(\tau_1) = j, \tau_1\leq E^\lambda 
%            	 \mid L(0) = \ell_{0}, \bs A(0)=\bs   a_{\ell_0,i}(x_0), \varphi(0) = i). \]
%	
%	Corollary~\ref{cor: a cor} gives an error bound between (\ref{eqn:m4sfkn}) and 
%	\begin{align}
%		\nonumber&\int_{x_1 = 0}^{\Delta-(x_0-y_{\ell_0})} h_{ij_1}^{+-}(\lambda,\Delta-(x_0-y_{\ell_0})-x_1) \int_{x_2 = 0}^{\Delta-x_1} h_{j_1k_1}^{-+}(\lambda,\Delta - x_2-x_1) \wrt x_1 \dots  
%	\\&\quad\times \int_{x_{2m}=0}^{\Delta-x_{2m-1}} h_{j_{m}k_{m}}^{-+}(\lambda,\Delta -x_{2m-1} - x_{2m}) \wrt x_{2m-1}h_{k_mj}^{++}(\lambda,\Delta -x_{2m})\wrt x_{2m}/|c_j|,
%	\end{align}
%	which is the Laplace transform of the time taken for the fluid queue to first exit \(\mathcal D_{\ell_0}\) on the event that it does so in phase \(j\in\mathcal S_+\), there are \(m\) changes of phase from \(\mathcal S_+\) to \(\mathcal S_-\) and \(m\) changes of phase from \(\mathcal S_-\) to \(\mathcal S_+\), and the phases immediately after these times are \(j_1,\dots,j_m\in\mathcal S_-\) and \(k_1,\dots,k_m\in\mathcal S_+\), respectively, given the initial phase is \(i\) and \(X(0)=x_0\). The events that there are \(m\) changes of phase from \(\mathcal S_+\) to \(\mathcal S_-\) and \(m\) changes of phase from \(\mathcal S_-\) to \(\mathcal S_+\), and the phases immediately after these times are \(j_1,\dots,j_m\in\mathcal S_-\) and \(k_1,\dots,k_m\in\mathcal S_+\), respectively, form a partition for \[\mathbb P(X(\tau_1) = x, \varphi(\tau_1) = j, \tau_1\leq E^\lambda 
%            	 \mid X(0) = x_0, \varphi(0) = i ). \]
%	
%	Using the same arguments which prove Lemma~\ref{lem:vn4} from Corollary~\ref{cor: a cor} proves the result. 
\end{proof}

The term \(\left[\left(\lambda \bs I-\bs T_{00}\right)^{-1}\bs T_{0+}\right]_{ki}\) is the Laplace transform of the time spent in phases \(\mathcal S_{+0}\) until the first time that there is a change of phase from \(\calS_{+0}\) to \(\calS_+\) and at this time the phase is \(k\in\calS_+\). This LST is the same for both the QBD-RAP and fluid queue -- the approximation models this time exactly. For sample paths which start in phase \(k\in\mathcal S_{+0}\), remain in \(\mathcal S_{+0}\) for some time, then transition out of \(\mathcal S_{+0}\) to some phase \(i\in\mathcal S_+\) we append (\ref{eqn: alkgbv}) to the beginning of (\ref{eqn: approx end conv lst*}).
